Research on Factory Fires in the Public Concession in the Last Six Years 117

The Municipal Council has a report on the Zhengtai Rubber Factory explosion, so it is worthwhile to research the records of factory fires in Shanghai. According to the Fire Department's records, from 1927 to 1932, in the 3,404 fire and accident alarms, factories were the location of 391 incidents, accounting for 11.5 percent. The property losses were also greater for factories than for other items, accounting for 28 percent of the total amount. In 1927 alone, factory losses accounted for seven-tenths of the total fire losses, amounting to approximately 750,000 taels. Since factories are places where many people gather, the risk of fire endangering lives is also greater. Fortunately, this was not seen much in these six years, but if the numbers for this year are included, the proportion will greatly increase. From 1927 to 1932, a total of 125 people died in fires, including 23 in factories, and 356 people were injured, including 82 in factories. The Zhengtai factory incident was fortunate to be an exception, but soon after, a similar tragedy occurred outside the concession, showing that the types of industries in Shanghai are becoming increasingly diverse, and many of them require dangerous goods, so the risk of death and injury is also increasing. The Fire Department has recently divided industrial fires into seven categories according to international practice for comparison: 1. Textile industry, 2. Chemical industry, 3. Public utilities, 4. Food and tobacco industry, 5. Iron and other metal industries, 6. Printing and paper industry, 7. Miscellaneous. Rubber factories have developed particularly rapidly in the last five years and have been proposed for separate statistics. Cotton mills have the most fire incidents, with 125 in six years, followed by printing and paper industries, with 68. Food and tobacco industries and metal industries are roughly equal, with 31 and 32 respectively. In terms of losses, flour mills are the highest, followed by yarn mills, then food and tobacco industries, and then printing and paper industries. In terms of loss of life, one person died in the printing and paper industry, and six in yarn mills. Silk mills had the most injuries, with 30, followed by yarn mills with 11, food and tobacco industries with 21, and printing and paper industries with 16. According to the records for 1927, there was only one rubber factory. There were no fires in this industry in the three years from 1927 to 1929. In 1930, there were three, in 1931 there were four, and in 1932 there were five. There were no deaths, and only three injuries. However, the records for this year will be very different. Factories often have dust-filled air, and if it contains combustible fibers, it is extremely dangerous. This is a recognized fact in the industrial world in other countries. If more attention is paid to management in Shanghai's factories, the loss of life and property can be greatly reduced. Looking at the records of factory fires in the past six years, it can be seen that strict official supervision is extremely necessary. In 1927, a flour mill on Yichang Road caught fire. The factory had two buildings, old and new, and thousands of bags of grain were stacked between the two buildings, and another 30,000 bags were stacked on the side of the new building facing the courtyard, so that the fire brigade's turntable ladders could not be used. When the firefighters could not stand inside the building (nine of them almost encountered danger), they had no choice but to stand by and watch it burn. In March 1928, a two-story Chinese-style cigarette factory near Bianer Road was carelessly remodeled. The factory building did not have a building permit. When the fire started, the female workers rushed to the stairs. One side of the stairs was a wall, and the other side was a board wall. The door opened inward, so 19 female workers were trapped and could not get out. After the fire brigade arrived, they broke through the wall and rescued them. Two of them died from their injuries. At the beginning of the following year, a female worker in a silk factory had a match in her pocket suddenly explode. Two thousand workers panicked and rushed to the commonly used large staircase. In fact, there were four other staircases, but because they were not trained, they did not know how to use them. When the fire brigade arrived, they could hardly get in because of the crowds. When the incident occurred, some of the female workers, including relatives of the firefighters, immediately shouted to the crowd not to panic, so those workers were the only ones who were not injured. Thirty-one people were injured and sent to the hospital, three died from their injuries, and many others had minor injuries. In May of that year, a metal shop and oil depot on Xinji Bang Road caught fire, killing ten people, all because they could not escape. In July, a printing shop on Baker Road with an unlicensed top floor caught fire. In August, a cigarette factory on Zhoujiazui Road was careless, and a lane next to it was blocked by objects, making rescue very difficult. In 1931, a printing factory on Qipu Road caught fire, and eleven people were injured after jumping out of the building. In October of the same year, a fire in a refining factory injured three firefighters. In the same month, a fire in a yarn mill on Yichang Road spread to an unauthorized mat shed outside the building. Hundreds of female workers fled for their lives, and each floor had only one unlocked door. After being rescued by the fire brigade, six people were dead on arrival at the hospital, and five were seriously injured.

Two Gangs of Boatmen Fight Over Dock Space 118

Changshu and Chongming Refuse to Yield

The two sides fought fiercely four times

The day before yesterday evening, in the Suzhou River, boatmen from Chongming and boatmen from Changshu clashed fiercely over dock space, engaging in four mutual brawls, resulting in injuries to many on both sides. The details are recorded below.

Chongming Gang Repels Changshu Gang: At 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, a Changshu cargo ship, captained by Xu Jinxiang, along with several crew members, sailed into the Suzhou River under the Jiangxi Road Bridge, intending to dock on the south bank to load tea. At that location, there were seven Chongming cargo ships connected together, preventing the Changshu ship from docking. Captain Xu Jinxiang became angry and strongly demanded that the Chongming ships yield the dock. The language was very intense and may have offended the Chongming ships. Shen Xigou and Yang Chuanfu, the captains of the Chongming ships, were angered by Xu's words and refused to move their ships. As a result, the two sides argued even more fiercely and refused to back down, leading to a sudden clash. Because the Chongming gang had more people, each holding bamboo poles and wooden sticks, they surrounded the Changshu gang. The Changshu gang could not resist the bamboo poles and sticks, and were all injured. Xu Jinxiang, Wang Louer, and Lu A'er were the most seriously injured, with broken heads and bleeding, and multiple serious injuries to their bodies. After persuasion from bystanders, they stopped fighting. The Changshu gang was filled with hatred and sought revenge. Considering it a great humiliation to be outnumbered and injured, they went ashore and gathered more people, returning to the ship at 5:00 PM to retaliate. As a result, the two sides clashed again, becoming more intense. Someone proposed peace, but the representatives of the two gangs refused to yield, and negotiations broke down. Before long, they fought again, and were persuaded by mediators to stop. However, after further arguments, it was still difficult to reach a peaceful resolution. The fourth clash then followed under the electric lights. At this time, there were many onlookers on both banks, and the enthusiasm for fighting on both sides grew stronger. The fighting lasted until nearly 7:00 PM, when water and land patrolmen arrived one after another after being reported. The crowds from both gangs scattered and fled, and Shen Xigou, the leader of the Chongming gang, intended to go ashore and escape, but was caught by the concession patrolmen. Western and Chinese patrolmen from the Customs Water Patrol also arrested Yang Chuanfu, Zhou Shuigang, Ning A'shi, Wang Feigang, Xu Xianggang, Gong Jinqi, and six others from the Chongming gang who had committed the assault, and sent the seriously injured Xu Jinxiang, Wang Louer, and Zhang A'er from the Changshu gang to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Both Gangs of Boatmen are Brought to Court: During the last battle, the clash was the fiercest, and many on both sides were injured. However, because there were no sharp weapons used during the fighting, there was not much bloodshed. When they caught sight of the patrolmen arriving, they fled in fear of punishment. After the Water Patrol detained the six arrested members of the Chongming gang, they continued to bring Xu et al. from the Changshu gang, who had finished bandaging in the hospital, back to the patrol station at 10:00 PM that night. At the same time, they sent personnel to the concession patrol station to transfer the leader of the Chongming gang, Shen Xigou, to be brought to justice for interrogation. They confessed to the circumstances of the clash, but the Chongming gang claimed that the Changshu gang had struck first and gathered hooligans to seek revenge, while the Changshu gang claimed that they were defeated because they were outnumbered, and that bystanders volunteered to go on board to help. The two sides' statements were contradictory. After taking their statements, the patrol station sent Detective Xue Silin at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon to send both sides to the local court to be prosecuted for disrupting waterborne security.

Murder Case Involving One Yuan 120

You Deming Owes Money, Refuses to Pay

One Punch Kills the Creditor

He Yongfang, a native of Rugao, residing at No. 18, Xiaozha Bridge Street, outside Xiaonanmen in the Nanshi district, was 26 years old. He made a living pulling a rickshaw. You Congming, a fellow townsman, 27 years old, lived with He. Previously, due to lack of funds, he borrowed one silver dollar from He. More than a month had passed, and he had not repaid it. Although He repeatedly demanded the money, You always claimed he had no money. On the 2nd of this month, He again asked You for the money, but You still replied that he had no money to return. He became very angry and started cursing. You also refused to yield, leading to a quarrel. In a fit of rage, You punched He hard in the waist. People intervened to stop the fight, and the matter subsided. The next day, He suddenly felt a dull pain in his waist. He went to a doctor for treatment. The doctor examined him and said that he had suffered serious internal injuries and that treatment would take a long time. He was shocked to hear this, fearing something unexpected would happen. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at around 2 PM, he grabbed You and reported him to Zhang Fengxiang, the guard at post number sixteen. Zhang brought him to the Third Section of the First District. After preliminary questioning by Chief Jin, the case was transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for investigation. The police from the section escorted the two to the court. The court detained You Deming and ordered He to return home first.

He was to seek medical treatment at the hospital and be summoned again when the court hearing took place. Unexpectedly, He's condition suddenly worsened when he returned home, and he died before he could be treated, at around 11 PM that night (the night before last). Yesterday morning at around 10 AM, Chief Jin learned of the incident and immediately dispatched Police Chief Wang Zuoxian to investigate. He also instructed Qin Defang, the local head of the Twenty-third Ward, to report to the court for an autopsy.

Details of the autopsy, etc., were previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday was the continuation of the inquiry.

According to the doctor's report, the autopsy revealed that the deceased had indeed miscarried a two- or three-month-old fetus. However, the cause of death was peritonitis. Mr. Guo informed the police of the above situation and inquired of Sheng whether he had had a relationship with the Gao woman. Sheng claimed that he had not. It was also possible that the deceased had engaged in physical relations with someone else. Mr. Guo concluded that the deceased, Gao Ruyi, died of illness before death, and the body was returned to Sheng Chunlan with a written guarantee for burial.

Closure of Bicycle Rental Shops in the French Concession 121

Protest Against Repair Tax

Electing Representatives to Petition

There are more than 40 bicycle rental shops in the French Concession of this city. In January of this year, the French Municipal Council, noting that these shops also engaged in repairs, sent officials to inform them that they had to pay for a repair license according to regulations, at the rate of three taels of silver per quarter. The shops believed that repairs were not the same as establishing a factory or employing workers specifically for repairs, but rather a matter of occasional parts replacement. Their capital was very small, and their profits were meager. Since they already paid for business licenses, they could not afford to pay for repair licenses. Therefore, they unanimously refused to pay. It is now known that the French Municipal Council is determined to implement the tax. Seeing the opposition from the industry, they cut off electricity to more than ten shops, including Fei Dian and Xia Fei, that refused to pay the tax. At the same time, they announced to all shops that they must pay for licenses by a certain deadline. Upon hearing the news, all the shops were panicked. Starting yesterday, all 40-odd shops closed down. They also convened a meeting to discuss countermeasures. The following resolutions were made: (1) Establish a joint office; (2) Elect five representatives to petition the local citizens' association and other organizations; (3) Petition the Party and government authorities to find ways to stop the tax; (4) Notify the industry to await a resolution; (5) If the purpose of abolishing the tax cannot be achieved, they are willing to close down permanently and never reopen.

China Merchants Public Bus Company Adds Special Express Bus Service Between North Station and Zhenru 122

China Merchants Public Bus Company Limited (decided to start from the 8th of this month) will add a new special express bus service on the North Station-Zhenru route. Yesterday, a special announcement was made to all sectors of society: We, the company, are responsible for the transportation in the northern part of the city. We have been operating diligently for four years. Although we have been affected by the economic crisis and the January 28th Incident, we have tried our best to maintain the business and facilitate transportation in order to assist in the commercial prosperity of the city. After investigation, the passengers on the North Station-Zhenru route (i.e., Route 3) include students, gentlemen, merchants, ladies, rural people coming to the city for business, and small vendors, all with different interests in the speed and convenience of transportation. In view of this, our company has purchased several new and sturdy chassis and installed modern bodies to ensure the carriages are elegant and the seats are comfortable. It is scheduled to start running special express buses on the morning of the 8th of this month (i.e., Saturday). The buses will run from the Baoshan Road North Station, along Baoshan Road, Gongxing Road, Zhongxing Road, and Jiaotong Road, directly to the entrance of Jinan University. Except for the two terminals, where passengers will be picked up and dropped off on time, the buses will not stop along the way. They will run back and forth every five minutes to live up to the name of special express buses. The buses will run from 7 AM to 7 PM every day. The fare is set at 20 cents per passenger. We hope that people from all walks of life will travel frequently and provide guidance so that we can continue to improve.

Hongzhen Fire Brigade Receives Newest Pumper Truck 123

Yuan Shixun, the director of the Hongzhen Fire Brigade, stated that although the area suffered from the January 28th Incident last spring, there were no significant casualties. A large test will be held on the 9th of this month.

Expansion of Pudong Electric Company 126

| Extending to the Seventh District of Nanhui County |

The towns of Beicai and Zhangjiangzha in the Seventh District of Nanhui County each originally had a power plant to supply electricity to the residents. However, due to their small scale and poor business, further expansion was not a fundamental solution. Therefore, local scholars and businessmen Gong Huibo, Huang Bingquan, Min Luxi, and others initiated a fund-raising effort of 25,000 yuan to form the Huibei Electric Co., Ltd., which would no longer generate electricity on its own, but would instead contract with Pudong Electric Co. to purchase electricity for redistribution. Pudong Electric Co. has installed seven British standard No. 16 three-phase high-voltage lines, starting from Tangqiao Town, passing through Yanjiaqiao Town, and reaching the Shangnan border near Wangjiazai, with a total of more than 120 poles planted. From the Shangnan border, Huibei Electric Co. extended the same type of high-voltage lines, passing through Diguqiao to Beicai Town, and then from Beicai Town extending the high-voltage lines, passing through Qianjia Catholic Church, to Zhangjiangzha Town, with a total of more than 240 poles planted. A 20 kVA transformer was installed in Beicai Town, and a 30 kVA transformer was installed in Zhangjiangzha Town, to supply electricity to the residents. This line project was also contracted to Pudong Electric Co. The original low-voltage lines in the two towns, which were extremely disordered, were also thoroughly reorganized. The work was completed and electricity was supplied yesterday (the 5th). The voltage immediately stabilized, the lights suddenly brightened, and electricity was supplied day and night, which was especially welcomed by the users. Therefore, those who had stopped using electricity due to dim lights and other inconveniences have been requesting reconnection one after another, and new users are applying for installation in an endless stream.

Bather Lin Zhu Dies Suddenly 128

Lin Zhu, a native of Wenzhou, nearly 50 years old, had held important positions in the military and political circles. He was currently a consultant to the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government, residing on Avenue Haig in Shanghai. The afternoon before yesterday, at around 3 PM, Lin went alone to the special room upstairs at the Quan Bathhouse at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and South Road for a bath. He had been sitting for less than a quarter of an hour when his complexion suddenly changed and he started vomiting blood non-stop. The bathhouse cashier immediately telegraphed the police and called a doctor from a hospital for an injection, but it was ineffective. He died a moment later. His family collected the body yesterday.

Across from the Huanlu Rainbow on Nanjing Road, the Shanghai National Goods Company was one of the earliest national goods companies established on Nanjing Road. Reader's Advisory

Discussion on "Can One Return to the Countryside?" 139

丨Letter from Mr. Liu Simin of This City丨

Mr. Reporter, I read the Reader's Advisory on April 4th, and I was puzzled for Mr. Xiongsheng, and for the entire Chinese society. Today I saw the title of the Reader's Advisory, saying that it was a discussion of "Letter from Mr. You Huaigao of the Free Farm Answering Mr. Xiongsheng in This Column," and I was very happy. In my heart I thought that Mr. You would definitely give us many new opinions, but as soon as I started reading his letter, I was disappointed. Mr. You said: "People who have lived in the city for a long time may feel a little bored and lonely, but I think that in this time of national crisis, seeing the city living a life of drunken stupor, it is better to find a quiet and lovely countryside to seek another way out, relying on my own ability to spend ten years building a new kind of Arcadia in my imagination." What a "new kind of Arcadia," what an "Arcadia in my imagination." Since our Mr. You is dreaming of this so-called "new kind of Arcadia in his imagination," why doesn't he try it himself, spend "ten years" trying it, close the door, make his good dreams, and enjoy his peace? Even if the Japanese army attacks, or some bandits attack, they won't patronize him, because the people in Tao Yuanming's "Peach Blossom Spring" "did not know there was a Han, let alone Wei and Jin." Mr. You's "new kind of Arcadia in my imagination" must be "did not know there was Zhou and Qin, let alone the Republic of China, did not know the Republic of China, let alone Japan, England, and the United States." In my opinion, since Peach Blossom Spring is so happy, it is better to persuade Mr. You to try it out first. First, how will people enjoy such a sweet and peaceful paradise, and second, it will never be as difficult for Mr. You as it is for Mr. Xiongsheng. The "200 yuan" loan is not a problem for Mr. You, but Mr. Xiongsheng has no way to get it (perhaps Mr. You will have mercy and lend him 200 yuan, which is another question), because he is a "pauper." Mr. You, pluck up your courage and do it well. As for the Japanese imperialists, they have only occupied the four northeastern provinces for the time being, and they won't be able to attack our Jiangsu for a while (?). The bandits in Jiangxi won't be able to share the produce of our Jiangsu for a while either. Even if they attack Jiangsu or share the produce of Jiangsu, your "new kind of Arcadia" will definitely be able to "stand alone," because it "did not know there was Zhou and Qin, let alone the Republic of China, did not know the Republic of China, let alone Japan, England, and the United States." Readers, don't think I'm joking, no, no. To be honest, Mr. You's thinking is a true reflection of the current Chinese bourgeoisie's attitude towards current politics, because the Chinese bourgeoisie is at a point where it cannot advance or retreat. To simply seek peace is what they wish for, but they cannot, or at least they are embarrassed to. To truly resist, to mobilize the whole country to resist, they dare not. His social relations and destiny have determined him. So he is wandering on the fork in the road, and there must be this kind of escapist fantasy, fantasy, fantasy. As for Mr. You's so-called "preconditions" and all other methods, they are all branch issues that arise from this fantasy. If we were to discuss them one by one, I am afraid that we would have to add twice as much space. Enough, enough, what does the teacher think?

Furthermore, Mr. You is "a person who advocates saving the country through rural education," so he is tirelessly "planning and strategizing" for Mr. Xiongsheng. Unfortunately, he does not know that in the current capitalist society, the countryside is dominated by the city, and no one can escape this common rule. Naturally, in another progressive society, that is, a socialist society, this common rule must be broken and the opposition between the city and the countryside must be eliminated. However, this is definitely not the business of the current society. America's large-scale agriculture and Japan's relatively small-scale agriculture are both typical of capitalist societies, but their rural areas are bankrupt and their panic is getting worse. I would like to ask, is their rural education not ten or a hundred times better than ours? Why are they still on the verge of collapse? Because the problem is not here. Mr. You's rural education is at most following in the footsteps of the United States, but the result will definitely not help their 1.2 billion or 560 million debts. There is another level. Mr. You only knows one thing, but does not know the other. For example, he said: "The benefits of the countryside... the people are honest, there is no deceit in the city." But that's not true. The people in the city are not the whole people. The upper class, monks, and bureaucrats only have power and money in their hearts. Their tongues are like swords and their intestines are like ice. Mr. You's criticism is correct, but for example, in Shanghai, the majority of the 3.2 million people (shop assistants, workers, and some young students) are still honest and trustworthy. Mr. You's eyes are colored, so he naturally cannot see this class, and I think his head may not have turned to this aspect. We want to remind him, "Turn around."

Reporter's note: The reporter thinks that Mr. You will definitely have more insights to reply after reading Mr. Liu's letter. We are waiting. However, the reporter wants to make a statement here. We have a fundamental view on the discussion of the readers, that is, from the partial problems to the general problems, from the branch problems to the fundamental problems. Mr. Xiongsheng said in his previous letter that he wanted to go to the countryside, but his purpose was only to seek personal life. Therefore, the reporter answered him, "In this situation, if you want to return to the countryside solely for the purpose of making a living, then we really cannot see any optimistic future." This sentence should emphasize the words "solely for the purpose of making a living." The implication is obvious, and it is especially recited for the readers.

1933 Soviet Russian Education Plan 141

Universities to Admit 30,000 New Students

Specialized Schools to Admit 150,000

(TASS, Moscow, 5th) The Russian Federation's education plan for 1933 was announced here today. It is said that this year, the Federation's universities will enroll 30,000 new students and graduate 9,000 students. Specialized schools will enroll 150,000 new students and graduate 58,000 students. Worker training classes will enroll 77,000 students and graduate 16,000 students. This year's funds for social and cultural undertakings total 232,000,000 rubles, of which 98,000,000 rubles will be used to provide for student expenses.

County People's Education Center Makes Northeast Three-Dimensional Map Model 155

Detailed Information on the Northeast for Public Viewing

Cooperation Personnel Training Class Has Begun

Four National Cloth Sales Offices Have Been Established

The Shanghai County Minhang County People's Education Center recently made a three-dimensional map model of the Northeast, which is displayed in the central tea garden for public viewing, and has established a cooperative personnel training class and four national cloth sales offices. The details are as follows:

Cooperation Personnel Training Class The first district cooperative established under the guidance of the center has been operating for two years and has been very effective in relieving the rural economy. Villagers from all villages have requested guidance and organization. Director Jin and Director Xi of the center, in addition to guiding the formal establishment of Huangfu Township, Li Dian Township, and Zigang Township in the first district in stages, also felt that there was a great shortage of cooperative personnel. Therefore, they specially drafted a simple charter, submitted it to the Education Bureau for approval, recruited elementary school graduates, and trained them for one month. Upon completion, they will be assigned to serve in cooperative societies in various villages. It is now heard that the class has started yesterday.

Northeast Three-Dimensional Map Model In view of the tense situation in the Northeast, the center, in addition to extracting important news from major newspapers and compiling them into wall newspapers, which are posted in various thoroughfares every day, recently designed a map and asked painter Gu Tifan to use clay, plaster, paint, and other materials to make a three-dimensional map model of the Northeast. On one side, it will write explanations of the customs, human feelings, products, and population of the three northeastern provinces and Rehe, so that the public can have a clear understanding of the situation in the Northeast after viewing it. It has now been made and displayed in the central tea garden, and the number of people going to visit it these days is very crowded.

National Cloth Sales Offices In order to relieve the rural economy, the center has specially stipulated the size, front, color, and style, and the first district cooperative will release white and colored yarn to rural women in various villages for spinning and weaving. The woven cloth will be sold by the marketing department on its behalf. It is now heard that in addition to the Aiqun Girls' School having purchased hundreds of bolts to be used for the school uniforms of the girls, it has also obtained the consent of Shanghai Wing On Company, the Mainland Department Store, the Zhabei National Goods Department Store, and the Penglai Market to sell it on their behalf.

Amateur Group A Pellet Shooting

Last Champion, Medinah, Lost Several Times 158

Yesterday's Results Were Only 47 Points Ahead

Highest Record of 169 Points

Liu Fuzong's Amazing Performance

丨Second Half Surpasses the Pellet King丨

丨Today, Li Gongying Meets Nie Kaor丨

Liu Fuzong is truly a master. Last champion Medinah was defeated in the preliminary round of the amateur Group A pellet shooting yesterday. At that time, there was still considerable room, and the loss of 47 points was not difficult to make up with one shot. We are abandoning talk of victory or defeat and talking about the facts. We feel that Liu's average stability is commendable. Medinah is of course an outstanding person, scoring 169 points in one shot, which is likely to be the highest record of this year's competition. Unfortunately, in the last few shots, his technique was flustered and he did not advance, almost ruining the big event. At the beginning of the competition, Liu's performance was good and he was often in the lead. He once led with 334 points to 256 points, but then he accidentally touched another pellet, which caused him to fall behind. Seeing Medinah score 169 and 33 points in a row, he finished the first half 500 points ahead, while Liu only had 361 points (a difference of 139 points). In the second half, Liu was able to confront the enemy and compete with each other at around 150 points. Until the end of the count, Liu's performance was particularly good, surpassing all the Shanghai pellet kings, including Medinah. The audience was amazed. If only the second half is considered, Liu actually won 92 to 00. Although the result was a loss of 953 to 1000 points, Liu can also be considered one of the masterpieces of his life. Today at 5:30 PM, our pellet king Li Gongying meets Nie Kaor. It is likely that Li will be able to cross the other side safely in calm conditions.

Shadow of the Standing Committee Meeting of Donghua Sports Association

Articles of Association 165

Name (1) The name of this association is Donghua Sports Association.

Purpose (2) To promote national health and various ball games and fitness exercises, as well as track and field sports, based on the principle of amateur sports, to train young people and strengthen their physique. Currently, the martial arts group and football group are organized first. When effective, various groups will be established gradually.

Members (3) All citizens of the Republic of China who are credible and have a considerable occupation may become members of this association. (4) Members of this association are divided into the following two types: A. Members without a fixed number, with the right to vote, the right to elect, and the right to be elected. B. Special members without a fixed number, with the right to vote. (5) All members of this association have the right to join various fitness exercises in each group. However, members who represent this association in competitions externally must be selected by the coaches of each group. They must abide by amateur sports rules and not receive any remuneration.

Membership Fees (6) The annual membership fees of this association are divided into two types: (A) Members pay an annual fee of 60 silver yuan. (B) Special members pay an annual fee of 5 silver yuan.

Membership Procedures (7) Anyone who wishes to become a member of this association must be introduced by two members or three or more special members, fill out a application form, and be approved by the committee before they can become a member.

Annual Meeting (8) This association holds an annual meeting once a year. (9) The annual meeting affairs are as follows: (A) Report on the annual progress. (B) Accounts and budget. (C) Elect the next committee. (D) Discuss all matters of reform of this association.

Meeting Notice (10) The date of the annual meeting shall be determined by the committee, and the secretary shall notify all members one week in advance.

Quorum (11) The annual meeting shall have a quorum of more than half of the members. If the quorum is not met, it shall be postponed to the same day and time of the following week, and the members present at that time shall constitute the quorum.

Honorary Chairman (12) This association shall publicly elect one honorary chairman.

Committee (13) This association shall establish a committee to preside over all affairs of this association. The number of committee members shall be fixed at 15 to 25. The election of committee members shall be conducted by all members at the annual meeting. The committee shall mutually elect one chairman, one vice-chairman, and five to seven executive committee members.

The chairman shall preside over the meetings of the committee. In the absence of the chairman, the vice-chairman shall preside. Resolutions shall be passed by a majority vote. In case of a tie, the chairman shall have the deciding vote. The committee meeting shall have a quorum of more than half of the members. The term of office of the committee members is two years, and they may be re-elected upon expiration. All committee members of this association are honorary positions.

Appointment of Staff (14) The staff of this association shall be appointed by the committee, including one secretary, one accountant, and physical education coaches for each group, to handle various affairs.

Clubhouse (15) The clubhouse of this association is temporarily located at 642 Jing'an Temple Road. Detailed Rules (16) The detailed rules for the office and accounting rules of this association shall be determined by the executive committee members.

Amendment of Articles of Association (17) If there are any matters not covered in these articles of association, they shall be discussed and amended at the members' annual meeting. (18) These articles of association shall be implemented upon approval by the general meeting of members.

Committee 166

Honorary Chairman: Minister Soong; Chairman: Mayor Wu; Vice Chairman: Shi Liangcai; Executive Committee Members: Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Shen Silang, Ding Xuetong, Sheng Pinchen; Committee Members: Guo Shun, Soong Tzu-liang, Wang Xiaolai, Zhao Jinqing, Zhang Jiongbo, Chen Guangfu, Liu Hongsheng, Liu Jisheng, Hu Yunzhuang, Wu Qiding, Zhou Wenrui, Yang Zhixiong, Li Yaosheng, Chen Shuyun, Shen Yiqing, Lu Yiming, Zheng Yangsheng, Shao Dabao.

Page 12

Spring and Autumn

Seizing Property 170

— Zhang Zhihen

There was a market town far from the city where all matters, large and small, were handled by the local gentry, without disturbing the officials. Let's talk about a family in the town who, due to an incident, offended the local gentry. The gentry were seriously angered and convened a general meeting in the town hall. Everyone discussed and said, "We must show this family who's boss." As a result, they agreed to have this family hand over all their property for them to manage. The farmland near Nan Village was to be managed by the gentry living nearby, nicknamed "Thirteen Fists." The family, being in a state of decline, had no one to speak for them and had to obey.

Years later, this Squire Jia had a disagreement with the other gentry over another matter. Angrily, he said to the gentry, "From now on, don't ask me about local public affairs. I don't want to go to the town hall anymore." Someone next to him said to Squire Jia, "Since you're closing your doors and not asking about local public affairs, then you should return the Nan Village farmland of the family you were managing." Upon hearing this, Squire Jia showed the full arrogance of a local bully, tilting his small melon-skin hat on his head, rolling up his sleeves high, pointing a finger at the person's nose, and saying, "The Nan Village farmland? That's another matter. My family is living off of it now. Return it? Don't even dream about it!"

Haha! It was only managing someone else's property, but who knew he would treat it as his own and seize it, living off of it. Isn't this a great joke?

The Japanese are now withdrawing from the League of Nations, but they consider the mandate over the former German colonies in the South Seas to be Japan's lifeline and refuse to hand it over. I wonder if there's any difference between them and Squire Jia, who seized property?

Courage Training 171

— Bicheng

When the Taiping Army occupied the areas of Suzhou, Songjiang, and Taicang, the Jiangsu gentry raised a large sum of money and hired foreign merchants' giant ships to transport Li Hongzhang's Huai Army to Shanghai. The special envoy for requesting troops was Qian Dingming of Taicang, the son of former Hunan Governor Qian Baozhen. Baozhen had friendship with Zeng Guofan, so Dingming was publicly recommended to enter Zeng's camp to request troops. Li Hongzhang was sent to Shanghai, and Dingming accompanied him. Soon after, when the fighting with the Taiping Army began, Hongzhang invited Dingming to observe. As they got closer, the bullets fired by the Taiping Army whizzed overhead. Hongzhang sat motionless, talking and laughing as if nothing were happening. Dingming suddenly lost his composure. Hongzhang smiled and said to him, "Bullets have eyes and don't injure people indiscriminately. Just relax and sit comfortably." Dingming's courtesy name was Diao Fu. Hongzhang had been through many battles and was naturally used to it; his courage training had reached a stage of pure skill. His saying that bullets have eyes and don't injure people indiscriminately was a rhetorical trick, probably a common saying he used to tell his subordinates. Later, Dingming repeatedly followed Hongzhang to supervise battles, gradually gaining courage. He accumulated military merit as a Juren (a successful candidate in the imperial examination) and also became a provincial governor.

A man from Suzhou, Zhu Yonghuang, entered the Yangtze River Navy Camp as a martial arts Jinshi (a successful candidate in the highest imperial examination) and practiced target shooting every day, never missing a shot. After returning to Suzhou, he followed a certain commander to Taihu Lake to suppress bandits. In a battle on the lake, none of the shots he fired hit their target, either flying too high over the bandit ships or too low, landing in the water before reaching the ships. The commander said to him, "You still lack experience and courage. When your heart races, your arms shake, and you can't aim accurately." Later, after repeated battles, he gradually became bolder, and his long-standing skill of never missing a shot when practicing target shooting was finally able to be displayed.

Judging from the above two incidents, courage training is indeed the most important task for a general. Since it's called training, it's naturally not something that can be accomplished quickly in one or two attempts. One must fight many battles and go through several fierce battles before having confidence. One must never harbor self-abandonment due to initial timidity and neglect to practice, ultimately leading to fleeing at the sight of the enemy, delaying national affairs, and ruining one's own reputation and career. This is something that those in military service must carefully consider.

Resume 172

— Zhu Lu

The more underpaid and poorly clothed the position is, the more difficult it is to get. Besides the written and oral tests, the most important thing is the so-called resume.

Because of the resume, Zhu was successful, and so it is even more difficult for a class of impoverished young men with genuine learning to get a small-paying teaching job in primary school, or a clerkship in an organization, than to ascend to Heaven. In this era of talent identification and selection, the impracticality of education and the lack of propriety in politics are still being loudly proclaimed from time to time in newspapers and in the mouths of the people. It makes this unqualified, impoverished person watching seem as preposterous as watching a Raymond Chandler mystery and wondering what the punchline is.

However, the resume of the great American inventor Thomas Edison was that of a primary school dropout and a newsboy... The resume of the great modern writer Maxim Gorky was that of a lawyer's clerk, a reporter for a newspaper, and a ticket seller for the telegraph... In general, they were complete vagabonds. Their resumes generally did not have the T.M. MR titles. However, how did their careers and literary fame startle the whole world instead? It makes this unqualified person even more perplexed.

Utterly bored, I pulled out a book of ancient prose to look at. "Bai Longxi was a commoner from cloth who drifted to the land of Chu and Han. At fifteen, he loved swordsmanship and visited the various lords. At thirty, he composed essays and strongly criticized the ministers..." Strangely, Li Bai, who took off his boots in the golden palace and composed Qing Ping Yue for the Tang Emperor, was actually such a sword-loving madman from Chu. "Generals and ministers are not born noble, a man should strengthen himself." "Heroes are not judged by their low origins." Even in the era of autocracy, there were such arguments. How is it that in this modern era of overthrowing feudalism, resumes are emphasized instead?

However, there are many remnants of XXX among the great men of modern times. I don't know how their resumes are written:

Carefree Words 173

— Ke Ding'an

Having left the solemn and frigid weather, we have now entered the mild and gorgeous season. According to most people, "This is the birth of the god of spring."

In the silent garden, due to the birth of the god of spring, the withered grass turned tender green; the withered trees became lush; the faded flowers became more vibrant, and the birds that had stopped singing resumed their songs... To the point that everything greeted the god of spring with great enthusiasm.

The god of spring was immensely pleased. It thought, "All the creatures on earth expect me and yearn for me in this way. I should give them the ultimate comfort." So it scattered the seeds of happiness among humanity.

乂　　乂　　乂　　乂

"Saving the country through aviation" is truly the only patriotic method this spring. The number of people who generously donated must be considerable. It is said: "Spending two yuan allows one to obtain a badge." Because spending two yuan allows one to obtain a badge, more and more people are donating.

The so-called modern people take this novel and unique badge to decorate themselves. For men, it is seen on the brim of the felt hat, on the left lapel of the long gown, on the left lapel of the suit... For women, it is seen on the short coat, on the long cheongsam..., one can see the small, novel, and unique badge of "Saving the country through aviation."

乂　　乂　　乂　　乂

Modern women welcome the arrival of the god of spring the most. They have now shed their bulky fur coats and put on light jackets. What is popular these days is a long cheongsam made of soft double crepe, covered with a short coat of matching color, or a light-colored short-sleeved long cheongsam paired with a woolen vest with an open front, or a short-sleeved pleated long cheongsam worn with a vest that is tightly fitted at the waist and about a foot long..., It is always necessary to match the climate and weather of spring in order to express the typified image of women.

乂　　乂　　乂　　乂

I have some leisurely friends who asked me to go to Longhua to see the peach blossoms long ago. It is said that they also brought sketching equipment. Seeing the peach blossoms is what I extremely desire, but I do not have the time, so I could not agree to my friends.

From seeing the peach blossoms, I thought all the way to the Northeast. Of course, I have never been to the Northeast in my short-sightedness, but I read the newspapers every day, so I have some influence. Recently, isn't the enemy army sneaking up on Dolun? Our General Feng Zhanhai is calmly fighting back. And Shimen Village, the intensity of the recent battles has not diminished the intensity of the January 28th Shanghai Incident and may even exceed it. Then Longhua, we can go to see the peach blossoms. The loyal soldiers there can only see the blood blossoms every day, seeing the splashing of blood blossoms!

Ah, god of spring! Which is more beautiful, the peach blossoms or the blood blossoms?

Chapter 3: Ultimately Failing to Untie the Knot and Visiting the Door to Make a Mistake, Secretly Pitying the Wish of the Young Maid to Share Food and Give Kindness

Zhao Weng laughed, "Don't let the conversation stray further and further. You should go back to the camp and not delay public affairs." Student Soldiers (Part Two) 175

— Ren Yu

Formal training begins tomorrow morning.

"Roll call"!

"All present"! Because this is the first day, there are definitely no absences, not even tardiness. Then:

"Attention"!

"Right face"!

"Forward"!

"Take large steps"!

··················

Dawn, to the next dawn, to the third day... It passed quickly like a movie. The weather gradually warmed up. The feelings between the soldiers and Mr. Sun gradually became harmonious. However, uh-oh! The sounds of talking and disobeying orders during drills gradually stirred up. And because the soldiers had never been on the front lines and faced bullets, their numbers gradually dwindled.

This kind of situation became more common:

"Cannonballs flying ahead! Kneel"!

Originally, the soldiers should kneel on the ground quickly and mechanically. But,

"Sir! I can't! The ground is too wet"!

"I can't! It's too dirty here! Like a dog pooped here"! "No! I can't kneel! My pants will tear"!

Also:

The squad leader nicknamed "Pretty Boy" also came to drill wearing a hybrid military-civilian outfit: On top, he wore a Western-style red sweater with a high collar turned up, and on the bottom, he wore a cloth military pants and leather boots.

"No way! Look at you! What is this mess! Change"!

"No"! Pretty Boy mourned with his pretty face.

"Why not"?

"I washed it last night, and it's not dry yet. I don't have a military uniform, and I'm not allowed to wear other clothes, should I come to drill naked"?

Yi! Huzzah! Huzzah! A burst of cheers thundered. Mr. Sun also laughed.

(IV)

Because there were so few soldiers, so few that it was a bit pitiful, they couldn't be a threat.

Mr. Sun! His mind was also flexible enough. He said: "The infantry manual is finished. Now it's time to teach the structure of guns and cannons." Back to the lecture hall.

Still trouble.

Mr. Sun did his best to draw a gun on the blackboard. "This is the barrel... this is the bolt... the safety device"...

But, sketching orchids, reading novels, talking, ... also created a smoky atmosphere.

(V)

"Hey! Why hasn't Mr. Sun been in the lecture hall for the past few days"?

"Maybe that old man from Hubei went to open a wonton shop"!

Indeed, Mr. Sun hasn't been here for several days. Go back to his hometown? No, he doesn't have a home in Hubei. Sick? Not likely either. And he didn't ask for leave from the school either. Hey! Really strange!

A month later.

"Military training officer Sun XX of XX school... used the name of Minister XX XX XX and requested a position from the XX Bureau of this city... It is confirmed to be forgery and is being charged with the combined crimes of deception and forgery and sentenced to imprisonment..."

Oh! So that's the kind of Mr. Sun! Finished! Finished!

"The Yellow Crane is gone, never to return! Only the great drill field remains here"! The soldiers simply sang it as their military song.

It was almost winter vacation.

Strange! Another disappearance: our big shot, our chairman, our student army preparatory member is also gone.

A few days later. The owner of the military clothing shop, Mr. Wang, brought a bill - a bill for over a thousand yuan, to our school. But no one came to accept it.

Free Talk

Special Badge 176

— Dasheng

Last year, I had a friend returning from studying in Germany, accompanied by another friend's German wife. It was the first time for this German lady to come to China, and of course, she couldn't understand the great mystery that China is. After arriving in Shanghai, they went to Nanjing together. When entering the city, the German lady saw that everyone entering the city had to have their luggage searched by the guards at the gate. Only my friend, I don't know what magic weapon he held up to the guards, immediately passed through safely, without the trouble of being searched. She was very surprised and asked:

"What is the reason for this?"

"Because I showed a special badge from a military organization to the guards, so I can be exempt from inspection," my friend explained. "So, with a military organization's badge, one can be exempt from any inspection?"

"That's how it is in China."

"Wonderful! Wonderful!" In the end, the German lady murmured to herself, expressing great surprise!

In fact, what's so surprising about this? In China, generals, lords, and even police officers, everywhere, have the "power" to take advantage. It goes without saying where "profit" lies, even in small matters like taking buses, boats, or going to the theater, they invariably take advantage. The reason is simple: Didn't the ancient sages and worthies say? "Those who govern are fed by the people." The meaning of being fed by the people is that a group of people is naturally entitled to take advantage, while another group is naturally meant to be taken advantage of. There's no need for "Wonderful!" in this.

An ancient saying also says: "The prince who violates the law is punished the same as commoners." Of course, this is just deceptive talk. Originally, it's hard to say what "law" is. Even if the prince truly commits a "crime," holding a "prince's" badge naturally entitles him to some advantage. For example, recently, it is said that Liao XX and four others were arrested simultaneously in Shanghai on suspicion of something. If we say that they are "guilty," then naturally all five are guilty. However, because Liao XX is the son of a martyr, someone gave him a badge that allows him to take advantage, so he was quickly released on bail, while the other four were eventually "sent to the capital for legal investigation."

Of course, we are not saying that allowing Liao XX to be released on bail is something that shouldn't have been done. We just feel that allowing bail because Liao XX is the son of a martyr is really strange. But Liao XX has already secured the advantage because he is the son of a martyr. As for the other four, when we think of the fact that many young people have disappeared without a trace after being sent to the capital in recent years, we can't help but worry about their future!

The revolution is said to have succeeded, and "people's rights" have also been listed as a classic for saving the world. However, "people's rights" are ultimately not as powerful as "military power" or "official power," and still rely on the protection of special badges. Thus, young people arrested simultaneously and in the same place are naturally destined to be released on bail or sent to the capital, legally investigated, or disappear without a trace. As for whether or not one needs to be inspected when entering Nanjing, that is ultimately a very small difference.

Empty Running 177

— Lin Weiyin

What exactly am I running for? Let me tell you.

Every time I go out, it seems I'm going to keep an appointment that I absolutely must keep, or to do something I absolutely must do. Before leaving, although I didn't think about where to go, once I'm out, there will always be a place that appears in my consciousness. So I go to that place I became aware of, as if there is someone I love to see waiting there, or something I prefer doing is taking place. When I arrive, as I should have imagined, I realize that there's nothing there. What's there is still ordinary people talking trivial nonsense. So I wait, waiting for the person I love to see and the thing I prefer doing, in the midst of that group of ordinary people talking trivial nonsense.

Among that group of people, I listen to them talk, and find it quite interesting. I listen intently, sometimes as if I am a member of that talking group or several groups, or every group. Sometimes, I don't hear anything they say, as if I am in a completely silent place. I am just me, solely me. I watch them come, watch them go; sometimes I suddenly see that a group at a table has changed, not knowing when the former group left and when the latter group arrived. But the person I love to see or the thing I prefer doing still hasn't arrived.

So I know I was wrong. If I hadn't come here but had gone to another place, I would have encountered the object of my desire. So I get up and go to another public place. But my desire still cannot be fulfilled, which doesn't seem surprising to myself. But what is my desire? Or, what is the person I love to see, what is the thing I prefer doing? This, I can't really answer. In fact, I'm not very clear. Or is it just running from one public place to another public place? I'm not very clear.

Yes, this is the ultimate purpose of my running.

Sketches of Avenue Joffre 178

— Zhou Lengjia

Avenue Joffre in spring is as dry as a desert. Every car that drives past kicks up a cloud of dust.

The sidewalks on both sides are full of foreign gentlemen and ladies with high noses, fashionable men walking arm in arm, and Pekingese dogs that eat twenty cents worth of raw beef every day.

The sun hangs obliquely on top of a seven-story building, and a French flag flutters in the air on top of it.

Several coolies pull a coal-laden cart, passing by on the road. Coal stains their faces, and sweat pours down their heads, like black devils. "Hang yu! Hang yu!" It makes one think of the Volga Boatmen's Song. At the intersection of Songshan Road, a row of five Vietnamese police officers stand guard, blue uniforms, pointed hats, rifles, creating an atmosphere of solemnity. People walking by feel a shiver in their hearts. In front of the Paris Grand Theater, two white cloth advertisements hang on the polished marble pillars on either side of the entrance. The advertisements are written with large characters about a foot in diameter: "Flower Butterfly." More people go in than there are flower butterflies.

The XX Electric Company, the five-tube radio in the window is broadcasting, broadcasting Wang Wuneng's "Crying for Old Uncle Du." A large circle of people surrounds it, listening.

Russian restaurants are competing for business, five cents for a soup, two dishes, and coffee.

"Dong! Dong! Dong!" "Tap! Tap!" A squad of Vietnamese soldiers turns from Luban Road and enters the barracks. At the intersection of Avenue Ferguson, a fire truck rushes past in front of a streetcar, high ladder, red body, the firefighters' brass helmets glinting in the sunlight. "Ming du du du!" Whizzing by, the ground vibrates.

Avenue Joffre, this is Avenue Joffre, filled with the contradictions of the current stage of capitalism.

The Origin of a Master 179

— By A. Maurois, translated by Wei Ke

(In recent years, the cry of "Master" within the country is deafening. Many people do not know the origin of such fellows. Having recently read a novel by Maurois, I saw this piece and hurriedly translated it to share with readers.)

When the novelist Grace walked into the studio, the painter Hunchback Stone was about to finish a still life painting: a few flowers inserted in a glass jar, a few mushrooms placed on a plate. Grace stared at her working friend for a while and said decisively:

| No.

The one who was working, surprised, raised his head and put down the work of embellishing a mushroom.

| No, Grace repeated, in a stronger tone, no, you will never succeed. You paint skillfully, you are quite talented, you are very honest. But your paintings are very ordinary, my child. Such paintings will not move people, will not arouse people's talk. In a salon displaying five thousand paintings, yours will never attract the attention of the sleeping audience... No, Hunchback Stone, you will never succeed. That's credible.

The Crossroads of Time and Love 180

— Zhang Ziping

"Bring me one of the steamed buns in that basket to eat."

"·····················"

Haiquan was relieved when he heard that. He hurried to the vegetable basket and took a big bean paste bun and gave it to Shiguang. Shiguang's mouth was covered by the big bun, and the room became quiet.

"Old Lin, bring me another one."

This really startled him, how could Shiguang eat so quickly. He went over again and picked one for Shiguang.

"·········Aren't you eating?"

Shiguang asked Haiquan while biting.

"I ate noodles this morning. Sister-in-law, aren't you eating?"

Haiquan asked Qiuying.

"I've eaten. ············"

"You've eaten? You ate on the road?"

"No. A friend invited me to a teahouse. ..."

This time she smiled at Haiquan very meaningfully again. Haiquan then thought, this woman is really more special than ordinary women, the child is sick at home, the husband is hungry at home, and she is still in the mood to go to the teahouse with friends outside to drink tea.

Thirty-two

Haiquan really slept on a military bed in Cao Shiguang's couple's room for three nights. The first night, he only heard the rustling sounds on their bed. He was so nervous that he didn't dare to cough, just endured his saliva and listened. At first, Qiuying advocated not turning off the lights. But Cao Shiguang advocated turning off the lights. Of course, Haiquan also agreed, because he knew that if the lights were on, all three of them might not be able to sleep. Haiquan's military bed was far from their bed, so of course he couldn't see anything. But Haiquan was always nervous, his spirit excited, and he couldn't sleep. By the third night, he thought that if he slept here for two more nights, he would definitely have neurasthenia, especially this night. He seemed to hear Qiuying's very slight chuckle. After he heard it, he couldn't sleep even more, but he had to pretend to snore loudly. He thought, if the pavilion room wasn't empty tomorrow, he would have to open a hotel outside. Even if it cost more money, he wouldn't hesitate.

When he got up the next morning, it was past nine o'clock. He only saw Qiuying changing the child's diaper. He didn't know where Shiguang had run off to.

| Why? Honest Hunchback Stone sighed. I do what I see, I don't expect anything else.

| But there is one more thing you have to pay attention to: you have a woman, my child, a woman and three children. Now milk is eighteen sous a liter, and eggs are one franc each. And there are more paintings than people who buy paintings, and there are more ignorant fools than people who know the goods. So, Hunchback Stone, what method do you have to stand out?

| Work?

| Don't joke. The only way to make these fools pay attention, Hunchback Stone, is to do something extraordinary. Spread the word that you are going to the North Pole to paint. Dress like an Egyptian king and wander outside. Found a sect. Mix some terminology together: such as the expression of force, and draw up some declarations. Deny movement or stillness, white or black, circumference or rectangle. Invent new Homeric-style paintings that can only distinguish between red and yellow, cylindrical paintings, octahedral paintings, quaternion paintings...

At this time, a strange and gentle fragrance announced the arrival of Mrs. Koslezusga. This was a beautiful Polish woman whom Hunchback Stone admired. She subscribed to some high-priced magazines, which spent a lot of money reprinting the masterpieces of three-year-old children; because she couldn't find the name of the honest painter Hunchback Stone in them, she looked down on his paintings. She leaned on the sofa, looking at the canvas that had already been started, shaking her golden hair, smiling with some regret:

| I saw yesterday, she said in a reed-like melodious tone, a modern black art exhibition. Ah! This kind of artistic sensibility, imagination and power! The painter turned a portrait of himself that he was satisfied with to show her.

| Not bad. She said casually, and then disappeared with her reed-like melodious tone, full of fragrance. Hunchback Stone threw the palette aside and fell on the sofa: "I'm going to change careers to be an insurance company auditor, a bank clerk, a police officer, etc. Painting is the lowest profession. Success is made by those fools. Only those conspirators can get it. Critics don't respect painters, but encourage those barbarians. I've really had enough of this, I won't do it anymore.

Grace listened to his words while smoking a cigarette, and considered for a while:

| Would you like to give these worldly people and pseudo-artists a deserved lesson? he finally said. Do you feel you have the ability to solemnly and mysteriously declare to Koslezusga and other aesthetes that you have been engaged in the innovation of your painting method for ten years?

| Me? Honest Hunchback Stone said in surprise.

| Listen to me... I will use two very eye-catching papers to tell everyone that you founded the Conceptual Analysis school. Before you, portrait painters only knew how to study people's faces. Unconscious things! This is not right. What truly represents a person is the concept he evokes in our hearts. For example, a portrait of a colonel is five huge sleeve badges horizontally arranged on a blue and gold background, with a horse painted in one corner and some medals painted in another corner. A portrait of a businessman is a factory chimney and a clenched fist placed on the table. Hunchback Stone, do you understand what you are going to give people? And can you paint twenty Conceptual Analysis portraits for me in a month?

The painter smiled quietly. (To be continued)

Commercial News 182

Finance

The Volatility of Gold Prices is Extremely High

New Price of 1,101 Yuan Appeared, Finally Rising 2.6 Yuan

Morning Opening Rose Due to Imposition of Export Silver Tax

Turned Down Due to U.S. Restrictions on Gold Hoarding

After-Market Continued to Rise Slightly Due to Germany's Plan to Abandon the Gold Standard

The gold market fluctuated greatly yesterday, initially rising and then falling. At the beginning of the morning, the overseas electricity reported that the silver slightly rose by 0.0625, the New York silver price increased by 125, the British-American and American-British exchange rates increased by 0.625 and 0.5625, the forward silver price increased by 0.5 cents and 1.5 mils, and the last two months fell by 1 mil and 1 cent. The American cotton rose by 5 pounds. Although not much, coupled with the Central Political Conference's resolution to abolish taels and change to yuan, and a 2.25% tax on all export currency materials, people's confidence improved. The gross price opened with a jump to 923 yuan. Hengyu, Fuchang, Richang, Chunyuan, Yongyi, Fengyong, and Junyong all bought in, rising to 978 yuan. At this time, a private telegram reported a increase of 125, slightly declining. By the time the market opened at 1,097.2 yuan, the exchange market opened slightly tighter, but because the U.S. government issued an order that each household could only hoard 100 yuan in gold, and any excess would be punished, which was no different from a gold ban, as people had cash of only 100 yuan per household, and the rest was paper money, a rise and fall began. The Guangdong gang still sold bars, the exchange market was slightly firmer, breaking the 90 yuan mark and falling to 1,088.3 yuan. Afterwards, the exchange market improved, and the July U.S. dollar rose from 29.5 yuan to 31.25 yuan, rising to a new high price of 1,101 yuan. Huabi offered 25 for the July U.S. dollar, and the noon closing was 1,098.7 yuan. The afternoon opening was 9.5 yuan, and the downward trend was still strong. Overseas electricity reported that the U.S. Treasury Secretary was collecting materials for a silver price meeting, Mumbai rose by two annas, and unfavorable news such as Germany's impending abandonment of the gold standard came, and the price fell to 90 yuan. Although it rose by more than 4 yuan due to the lack of a definite method in Germany, it broke 90 yuan to 89.5 yuan due to the sale of bars by the Jewish merchant Qiao Zhifu. The closing price was 1,090.2 yuan, with a red addition of 25.6 yuan at the beginning and a final addition of 21 yuan. The swap spread retreated from 12 yuan to 9 yuan, and the source of spot goods was endless. The market conditions of the day are recorded below:

The morning opening was 1,097.2 yuan, a rise of 9.6 yuan compared to the previous close, which was beneficial to the gold market due to the central news. The goods opened at 6.5 yuan, and the exchange market opened with British flat and American slightly tight. The near-term offer was British exchange at 1 shilling 8 pence 25, and the U.S. dollar at 28.8125 yuan, which was not satisfactory, so it gradually fell back from 7.6 yuan. In addition, the overseas environment was not good, and Fuyu, Zhifeng, and Yong all sold. Sugar Market: Measures for Abolishing the Tael and Adopting the Yuan in the Sugar Industry 196

Yesterday, the sugar market saw the auction gold price increase again, with a tightening trend. The Sugar Industry Association's division of the market for abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan was implemented yesterday. Therefore, the Sugar Industry Association decided on several measures for changing to the yuan system as follows: "(1) All sugar markets will implement the abolition of the tael and the adoption of the yuan starting today. (2) The unit of yuan for incoming and outgoing goods will be in cents. Five li or more will be rounded up to one cent, and less than five li will not be counted. (3) The labor fee on this street will be changed to $0.14 per dan, with a 10% discount. The guest group labor fee will be changed to $0.17 per dan, with a 3% discount. (4) The customs inspection fee will be changed to $0.04 per dan, with a 50% discount. (5) The price of unbagged refined sugar sold according to the tael standard should be converted to yuan at an exchange rate of 715. (6) The money for goods sold before today will be converted to yuan at an exchange rate of 715 on April 5th. (7) Invoices issued by merchants will be calculated in yuan from today onwards." As a result, sugar prices have also been changed to yuan pricing. Ordinary grade 24 coarse granulated white sugar was priced at $21.15. Later, it was divided at $21.12, slightly higher than before. No. 20 medium granulated white sugar was priced at $20.04. Guanghua Factory opened by Changxing was selling 50 bags of powdered sugar at $21.68. Lu Zi cotton white sugar was at $21.4, and Shou Zi sugar was at $20.098. Chao groups opened authentic Shang Bing white sugar at $21.82, about 3 jiao higher than before. This factory's car ice No. 1 was opened at $24.7, and No. 2 was at $24.7. Zhenxin opened Binghuaqing at $16. (Yesterday's report listed the Hechi futures price as $3.775, and the character "三" was misprinted as "一". It should be corrected.)

Our Army Reclaims Haiyang Town Again 199

Enemy Suffers Heavy Losses and Collapses

Our Army Pursuing and Attacking Across the Tang River

Enemy Reinforcing Along the Liujiang Road, Preparing a Counterattack

(Luanzhou) After the vanguard positions in Wangjialing, Lipanzhuang, and Daliying were successively recaptured, reinforcements joined the front line and continued the counterattack. At 7 PM on the 6th, Haiyang Town, which had been lost for the second time on the night of the 5th, was completely recaptured, greatly boosting the morale of our army. The enemy collapsed and disintegrated. They are now being pursued and attacked across the Tang River. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

(Luanzhou) After the capture of Haiyang, the enemy launched repeated attacks in an attempt to break through our main position west of Haiyang, encircling Qinhuangdao from three sides and forcing our army to retreat backward. The past two days have been critical for the Luan East war. He Zhuguo revealed the enemy's ambitions and hastily transferred new strength troops of his army from Luan overnight to the front line to consolidate the position, defend Qinhuangdao, and counterattack lost ground. From 9 PM on the night of the 5th, the enemy attacked along the Ping Shangying line in the Haiyang Town area. At 10 PM, more than 600 enemies infiltrated the southern end of Haiyang and attacked, breaking through the vanguard positions of Wangjialing and Wujiazhuang. We waited at ease and firmly defended the main position. At dawn on the 6th, the former cavalry regiment's Lieutenant Colonel Liu's infantry battalion launched a surprise and fierce counterattack. The 3rd Company of Liu's regiment recaptured Wujiazhuang, and the Ba battalion, in cooperation with the 4th Artillery Company, recaptured Wangjialing. The enemy fled in panic. In this battle, more than 20 soldiers were wounded, and Li Shengda, the company commander of the 3rd Cavalry Company, was injured. The enemy's casualties exceeded ours several times over. At dawn, another enemy force attacked Lipanzhuang on the Ping Shangying line. After our Ding Battalion cooperated with the artillery in a counterattack, the enemy's artillery fire was very intense. Our artillery fire was also concentrated to cover the fierce attack, followed by hand-to-hand combat. At noon, the enemy was finally repelled, and the Lipanzhuang vanguard position was completely recaptured, greatly boosting morale. Reinforcements also arrived at their destination and continued the counterattack. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

(Luanzhou) A secret report revealed that the enemy on the eastern front consisted more of puppet troops than Japanese troops. He asked him to resign together at an appropriate time. At the same time, the cabinet used its authority to ask him to reconsider his resignation.
